                                                               iv
INTRODUCTION
SECTION 1.
STUDY PURPOSE

The purpose of this study is to quantify and analyze the traffic impacts of a proposed 180 student private
school to be located at 2323 Euclid Avenue, the site of the Redwood Baptist Church, in Redwood City.
See Figure 1, Location Map, page 2.

ANALYSIS METHODOLOGIES

Six intersections have been designated for analysis in this study. They are ­
      1) Connecticut Drive & church driveway
      2) McGarvey Avenue & Euclid Avenue
      3) McGarvey Avenue & Connecticut Drive
      4) Roosevelt Avenue & McGarvey Avenue
      5) Roosevelt Avenue & Connecticut Drive
      6) Alameda de las Pulgas & McGarvey Avenue

The six designated study area intersections have been analyzed according to the methodologies
contained in the 2000 edition of the Highway Capacity Manual. Using the TRAFFIX1 network
modeling program a traffic network model was created to analyze the streets and intersections within
the project study area.

ANALYSIS SCENARIOS

Four scenarios have been developed and analyzed in this study.

1.   Existing Conditions. Current (2012) traffic volumes within the study area.

2.   Background Conditions (Existing + Pending Projects). Background traffic is that traffic
     expected to be present at the time the project is ready for occupancy. It consists of existing traffic
     plus traffic to be generated by those developments that are anticipated to be built and occupied by
     the time the project is ready for occupancy.

3.   Project Conditions. (Existing + Project and Existing + Pending + Project) Project trips are
     estimated based on the proposed land use and are then added to Background Conditions traffic in
     order to obtain the Project Conditions traffic scenario. An Existing + Project scenario is also
     included to comply with a recent State Supreme Court ruling.

                            

                                                                        
4.   Near-Term Cumulative Conditions. (Existing + Pending + Future Development) Cumulative
     traffic is that traffic expected to be present within the next six years. It consists of existing traffic
     which has a % per year growth factor applied, plus trips from pending projects and trips from
     near-term future development projects within the study area. This scenario is analyzed without
     and with the project.




                                                      3
EXISTING CONDITIONS
SECTION 2.
ROADWAY NETWORK

Alameda de las Pulgas. This street is classified as a Connector Street in the Redwood City
General Plan and is generalized as street with moderate to high through traffic. The street has
bike lanes and parking on both sides and is 2-lane, divided street running generally north-south
through the project study area.

Roosevelt Avenue. Roosevelt Avenue in the project area is a 2-lane street with parking allowed
on both sides. The street is classified as a Bike Boulevard in the Redwood City General Plan. A
Bike Boulevard is characterized as a through route for cyclists and provides priority to bicycling
along the route.

McGarvey Avenue. This street is a local street running east-west through the study area with
two lanes and parking allowed on both sides. Even though it is a local street it carries a higher
volume of through traffic than a typical local street.2

Euclid Avenue. Euclid Avenue is a 2-lane local street from Upton Street to the project site with
parking generally allowed on both sides.

Connecticut Drive. This 2-lane local street has parking generally allowed on both sides of the
street and runs generally north-south between McGarvey Avenue and Massachusetts Avenue.

INTERSECTION LANE CONFIGURATIONS

The lane configurations and controls of the six study area intersections are shown on Figure 2,
Existing Intersection Lane Configurations, page 5.

EXISTING TRAFFIC CONDITIONS

Traffic Volumes. Existing 2012 peak hour traffic volumes through the study area intersections
are shown on Figure 3, Existing Peak Hour Traffic Volumes, page 5. Peak hours for purposes of
this study are those that occur between 7 and 9 a.m. 2:30-4:00 p.m., and between 4 and 6 p.m. on
an average weekday. See Appendix A for traffic count data.

LEVELS OF SERVICE DEFINED

LOS (Levels of Service) methodologies are described in Section 1. Levels of Service define how
well or how poorly a traffic facility ( a street or an intersection) is operating. There are by
definition six Levels of Service. These definitions are presented in Table A on page 7.

                                 TABLE A: Levels of Service Definitions
                          for 2-Way and All-Way STOP Controlled Intersections
  Level of Service                                         Traffic Conditions
            A               Very low delay, less than or equal to10.0 seconds of average control delay per
                            vehicle.
            B               Average control delay in the range of 10.1 to 15.0 seconds per vehicle
            C               Average control delay in the range of 15.1 to 25.0 seconds per vehicle
            D               Average control delay in the range of 25.1 to 35.0 seconds per vehicle
            E               Average control delay in the range of 35.1 to 50.0 seconds per vehicle
            F               Average control delay in excess of 50 seconds per vehicle.
Reference: Highway Capacity Manual, Chapter 17, HCM2000.


LEVELS OF SERVICE STANDARDS

The City of Redwood City Level of Service standard is D for unsignalized intersections.

EXISTING CONDITIONS LEVELS OF SERVICE

Levels of Service have been calculated for the existing conditions scenario using the analysis
methods contained in the 2000 Highway Capacity Manual. The results of the LOS calculations
are summarized in Table B on page 8. All of the controlled approaches of all of the intersections
operate at LOS C or better during the three peak hours of the day. The calculation worksheets
are provided in Appendix B. The LOS calculations reflect traffic conditions existing in 2012.

                                                                       8
BACKGROUND CONDITIONS
SECTION 3.
Background Conditions are those traffic conditions which are expected to occur immediately
prior to the completion and occupancy of the proposed school. Traffic from developments that
are approved and/or ones that are expected to be completed and occupied prior to the proposed
project is added to existing traffic volumes to create this traffic analysis scenario.

APPROVED PROJECTS

For purposes of this study there are two projects that could be completed prior to occupancy of
this project. They are:

     1)      The Roosevelt Elementary School will expand to a K-7 school in 2012-2013. The
             expansion will add 110 students to the existing 490 students presently enrolled.3

     2)      Roots N Wings Montessori School on the Redwood Baptist Church site enrollment to
             40 students, the maximum permitted by the State license.

Projections of vehicle trip generation for these two schools are provided in Appendix C.

BACKGROUND CONDITIONS PEAK HOUR TRAFFIC VOLUMES

Peak hour traffic volumes at the six designated intersections are shown on Figure 4 page 10, for
the Background Conditions scenario.

BACKGROUND CONDITIONS LEVELS OF SERVICE

Levels of Service have been calculated for the background conditions scenario using the analysis
methods contained in the 2000 Highway Capacity Manual. The results of the LOS calculations
are summarized in Table C on page 11. The calculation worksheets are provided in Appendix B.

Only a slight change in delay or V/C ratio results when background trips are added to the
roadway network. At the Roosevelt Avenue & Connecticut Drive intersection during the PM
street peak hour the delay decreases slightly and this is due to the fact much of the added traffic
is right-turning and, therefore, has a lower delay than the through or left-turning traffic.

                                                                       11
PROJECT CONDITIONS
SECTION 4.
PROJECT DESCRIPTION

The project is a 180 student private elementary school on the site of the Redwood Baptist
Church at 2323 Euclid Avenue.

PROJECT VEHICLE TRIP GENERATION

The estimate of vehicle trips to be generated by the project is shown in Table D below. The
estimate is based on a synthesis of arrival and departure times for students and staff . The AM
Street Peak Hour is between 7 a.m. and 9 a.m., the mid-afternoon peak hour is between 2:30 and
4:00 p.m., and the PM Street Peak Hour is between 4 p.m. and 6 p.m. It is assumed that 5% of
the students will walk to and from school, and that 25% of the students will car pool. A detailed
trip generation table can be found in Appendix C.

                           Table D: Trip Generation for 2323 Euclid Avenue
                                           Private School

                                                        Rates                      Volumes
                                  Peak
 Facility       Size   Units      Hour        In        Out      Total       In      Out     Total

                                  AM         0.73       0.54     1.27        132     98      230

 K-8            180    STDNT     MID PM      0.56       0.49     1.05        101     88      189

                                   PM        0.07       0.10     0.17        13      19       32


PROJECT VEHICLE TRIP DISTRIBUTION

Project vehicle trips have been distributed on the basis of likely student residency in an area
from 0 to 10 miles distance on the peninsula. The assumed vehicle trip distribution is shown on
Figure 5, Project Vehicle Trip Distribution, page 13.

PROJECT PEAK HOUR TRAFFIC VOLUMES

The Project Conditions (Existing + Approved + Project) peak hour traffic volumes at the six
study area intersections are shown on Figure 6, Project Peak Hour Traffic Volumes, page 14.

PROJECT CONDITIONS LEVELS OF SERVICE

Levels of Service have been calculated for the project conditions scenario using the analysis
methods contained in the 2000 Highway Capacity Manual. The results of the LOS calculations
are summarized in Table E on page 15. The calculation worksheets are provided in Appendix B.

                                                                       15
CUMULATIVE CONDITIONS
SECTION 5.

CUMULATIVE CONDITIONS SCENARIO

The Cumulative Conditions scenario for purposes of this study are those that are expected to
occur within the next six years. The city has identified development projects throughout the
city, but none will contribute quantifiable traffic through the project study area. In a review of
traffic counts at some of the study area intersections over the past five years that volume of
traffic has remained static or as diminished slightly. However, to take into consideration
development growth throughout the city, a growth factor has been applied to the existing traffic
volumes at the rate of 0.5% per year for the next six years. One development has been identified
in the project area and that is the expansion of the Roosevelt Elementary School to K-8. That
change will occur in the 2013-2014 school year and will add an additional 50 students to the
school.

Projections of vehicle trip generation are provided in Appendix C.


CUMULATIVE CONDITIONS PEAK HOUR TRAFFIC VOLUMES

The cumulative traffic volumes are shown on Figure 7, Cumulative Peak Hour Traffic Volumes,
page 17, and the Cumulative + Project Peak Hour Traffic Volumes, Figure 8, are shown on page
18.


CUMULATIVE CONDITIONS LEVELS OF SERVICE

Levels of Service have been calculated for cumulative conditions scenario using the analysis
methods contained in the 2000 Highway Capacity Manual. The results of the LOS calculations
Are summarized in Table F on page 19. The LOS of the westbound approach of McGarvey
Avenue at Roosevelt Avenue reduces from C to D during the morning street peak hour. All of
the other controlled approaches at the other intersections operate at LOS C or better during all of
the peak hours evaluated.

                                                                       19
SITE ACCESS, CIRCULATION AND PARKING
SECTION 6.

SITE PLAN

The site plan is shown on page 21, Figure 9, Site Plan. The school will be utilizing facilities and
grounds on the church site for classrooms and outdoor activities. The Roots N Wings
Montessori School occupies the classroom building at the south end of the property.

SITE ACCESS

Access to the site is via a driveway connection from Connecticut Drive or at the end of Euclid
Avenue. At both locations ingress and egress are permitted.

CIRCULATION

The Cambridge Academy proposes to make the aisle along the west side of the church one-way
south to north with vehicles entering from Connecticut Drive and exiting out onto Euclid
Avenue for student drop off and pickup. The plan also proposes to make the driveway
connection to Connecticut Drive one-way in only.

The critique comments of the site plan are shown on Figure 10, page 22. The connection to
Connecticut Drive should be maintained as a 2-way aisle so that traffic to and from the
Montessori school would not have to circulate through the entire site to exit. This will require
modifying the parking to perpendicular on the north side and parallel parking on the south side
of the 55 ft. wide corridor. That will reduce the number of parking spaces in that area from 22 to
19, a loss of three spaces.

The intersection where Cambridge Academy traffic and Montessori school traffic divide should
be kept clear so that the Montessori school traffic can exit without being blocked by Academy
traffic. This can be done with signs and pavement markings.

The aisle on the west side of the property needs to be at least 17 feet wide to permit parking
while maintaining a minimum 10 foot wide aisle. There is space for passenger drop off and
pickup for 15 vehicles. To accommodate the inrush of vehicles in the morning the idle time for
vehicles has to be held to a minimum so that the queue of vehicles does not spill out onto
Connecticut Drive or Euclid Avenue. The school director, Carol Berg, has indicated that the
staff will assist the students exiting the vehicles and that the parents will not be allowed to park
for any length of time during the drop off in the morning or pick up in the afternoon.




                                                 20
   

   
"

!
#

!


















                        $

                        %
  
  &
          

         




               !!

         




              

          




     

     

     



                    

                     
Picking up students in the afternoon will take longer because the student (s) has to be matched
with the right vehicle at it enters and parks on the site. A plan to address student drop off and
pickup should be prepared by the school and approved by the city to preclude blocking queues
from encroaching into Connecticut Drive.

PARKING

The site plan shows 101 designated parking spaces including four handicap spaces. During
school hours up to 31 spaces could be blocked off and the areas used for outdoor student
activities. The data on peak parking demand for elementary schools is very limited. An
estimate of the peak demand is 0.2 parking spaces per student.4 For the Cambridge Academy
this equates to a peak demand of 36 parking spaces. There appears to be an adequate number of
parking spaces on the site to support the school's parking demand as well as that of the Roots N
Wings Montessori School.

There is one designated parking space on the easterly side of the site near the existing
playground that is inaccessible and should be eliminated. Also, the 12 parking spaces on the
one-way aisle at the northwest corner of the site need to be reversed from their current
configuration so that vehicles on the aisle can access these spaces. During times of student drop
off and pickup these parking spaces should be closed off.




                                                         23

       4
           Institute of Transportation Engineers, Parking Generation, 4th Edition, © 2010
CONCLUSIONS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
SECTION 7.

CONCLUSIONS

The Cambridge Academy private school is projected to generate 230 vehicle trips during the
morning street peak hour but only 32 vehicle trips during the afternoon street peak hour. The
school peak hour in the afternoon is 3:00-4:00 p.m. and during that hour the school is projected
to generate 189 vehicle trips. There were six intersections included in the study and at none of
these intersections did project added traffic create a significant quantifiable impact.


RECOMMENDATIONS

Off-site:

None.

On-site:

1)   Modify the site parking and aisleways as shown on the Site Plan Critique, Figure 10, page
     22.

2)   Prepare a plan for handling student drop off and pickup during the morning and mid-
     afternoon peak times to preclude the queue of vehicles spilling over onto Connecticut
     Drive or Euclid Avenue. This plan to be submitted to the city for review and approval
     prior to the opening of the school.




Richard K. Hopper, P.E., PTOE
Principal
